- E = -3.0564119369598 * 0.0825581177584772 Ōēł -0.25236...

The key basis functions in GT are: **x, v, sin(t), v┬Ęx┬▓, x┬Ę|v|^(1/3)**

Now I need to check which candidates can represent these 5 basis functions.

The critical question for many candidates is whether `x*log(c6*|v| + 1)` or `x*|v|` or `v^c8*x` or `(c8+v)^c9*x` can substitute for `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

**Key observations:**
- `log(c6*|v| + 1)` is NOT equivalent to `|v|^(1/3)` for any constant choice (different functional forms - log vs power)
- `|v|` is NOT equivalent to `|v|^(1/3)`
- `v^c8` with c8=1/3 gives `v^(1/3)`, but this is NOT `|v|^(1/3)` when v < 0 (since v takes both signs). `v^(1/3)` for negative v gives a negative real cube root, while `|v|^(1/3)` is always positive. So `v^(1/3)*x` ŌēĀ `|v|^(1/3)*x` for negative v.

Wait - let me reconsider. The GT has `x*|v|^(1/3)`. For `v^c8*x` with c8=1/3: in real arithmetic, `v^(1/3)` for negative v = `-|v|^(1/3)`. So `v^(1/3) = sign(v)*|v|^(1/3)`. This is NOT the same as `|v|^(1/3)`.

However, `(c8+v)^c9` is also not `|v|^(1/3)`.

None of the candidates with `log`, `|v|`, `v^c8`, or `(c+v)^c` can exactly match `|v|^(1/3)` since v takes both signs.

Wait - but could combinations of terms work? For instance, `x*|v|` combined with other v-dependent terms? No, `|v|` and `|v|^(1/3)` are fundamentally different functions.

Since `|v|^(1/3)` cannot be represented by `log(c*|v|+1)`, `|v|`, `v^c`, or `(c+v)^c` (given v takes both signs), **none of the candidates can match the GT**.

Let me double-check: Is there any candidate that directly has `|v|^(1/3)` or equivalent? No candidate contains `Abs(v)**c` as a standalone factor multiplied by x.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none can produce the term `x*|v|^(1/3)` exactly. The candidates use `log(c*|v|+1)`, `|v|`, `v^c` (which gives `sign(v)*|v|^c` for fractional c), or `(c+v)^c`, none of which equal `|v|^(1/3)`.
